<small><img alt="Portal" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fd/Portal-puzzle.svg/16px-Portal-puzzle.svg.png" title="Portal" width="16" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fd/Portal-puzzle.svg/24px-Portal-puzzle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fd/Portal-puzzle.svg/32px-Portal-puzzle.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="32" data-file-height="28" /> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Rohingya_people&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Portal:Rohingya people (page does not exist)">Portal</a> <img alt="WikiProject" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/People_icon.svg/16px-People_icon.svg.png" title="WikiProject" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/People_icon.svg/24px-People_icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/People_icon.svg/32px-People_icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="100" data-file-height="100" /> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikipedia:WikiProject_Rohingya&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Rohingya (page does not exist)">WikiProject</a><br />
<img alt="Category" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/48/Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg/16px-Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg.png" title="Category" width="16" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/48/Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg/24px-Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/48/Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg/32px-Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="36" data-file-height="31" /> <a href="/wiki/Category:Rohingya_people" title="Category:Rohingya people">Category</a> <img alt="Commons page" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Commons-logo.svg/12px-Commons-logo.svg.png" title="Commons page" width="12" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Commons-logo.svg/18px-Commons-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Commons-logo.svg/24px-Commons-logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="1376" /> <a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:Rohingya_people" class="extiw" title="commons:Category:Rohingya people">Commons</a></small></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%">
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Rohingya_people" title="Template:Rohingya people"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Rohingya_people&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Template talk:Rohingya people (page does not exist)"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Rohingya_people&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A series of violent clashes have been ongoing in the northern part of <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Rakhine_State" title="Rakhine State">Rakhine State</a> since October 2016. The violence has been characterised by attacks against <a href="/wiki/Rohingya_people" title="Rohingya people">Rohingya Muslim</a> <a href="/wiki/Civilian" title="Civilian">civilians</a> by Myanmar's military and the local <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Myanmar" title="Buddhism in Myanmar">Buddhist</a> population,<sup id="cite_ref-satellite_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-satellite-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MyanmarDeniesRape_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MyanmarDeniesRape-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aung_san_skip_20170913_npr_org_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aung_san_skip_20170913_npr_org-15">[15]</a></sup> as well as armed clashes between the government forces and Rohingya insurgents of the <a href="/wiki/Arakan_Rohingya_Salvation_Army" title="Arakan Rohingya Salvation Army">Arakan Rohingya Salvation Army</a> (ARSA). The conflict has sparked <a href="/wiki/International_reaction_to_the_2016%E2%80%9317_Rohingya_exodus" title="International reaction to the 2016–17 Rohingya exodus">international outcry</a> and was described as an <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnic cleansing</a> by the United Nations High Commissioner for Human Rights.<sup id="cite_ref-aung_san_skip_20170913_npr_org_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aung_san_skip_20170913_npr_org-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> In August 2017 the situation intensified and hundreds of thousands of refugees fled Myanmar into <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, with an estimated 429,000 refugees having arrived by 22 September 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-un_secretary_gen_2017_09_13_cnn_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un_secretary_gen_2017_09_13_cnn-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Muslim <a href="/wiki/Rohingya_people" title="Rohingya people">Rohingya minority</a> in the region has <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims_in_Myanmar" title="Persecution of Muslims in Myanmar">historically experienced persecution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bad_to_worse_2017_09_06_washpost_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bad_to_worse_2017_09_06_washpost-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GuardianUN_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuardianUN-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pope_laments_2017_08_27_ap_foxnews_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pope_laments_2017_08_27_ap_foxnews-21">[21]</a></sup> Laws such as the 1982 <a href="/wiki/Myanmar_nationality_law" title="Myanmar nationality law">Myanmar nationality law</a> ban Rohingya people from obtaining citizenship and since Burmese independence from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, over a dozen rounds of attacks against Rohingya have led to their dislocation from much of Rakhine State.<sup id="cite_ref-Selth_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Selth-22">[22]</a></sup> Most recently the <a href="/wiki/2012_Rakhine_State_riots" title="2012 Rakhine State riots">2012</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2013_Myanmar_anti-Muslim_riots" title="2013 Myanmar anti-Muslim riots">2013</a> attacks caused mass displacements.</p>
<p>The current conflict began in October 2016 when ARSA insurgents attacked Burmese border posts along the <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>-<a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a> border. In response, Myanmar authorities launched a military campaign against the Rohingya and from October 2016 to June 2017, government operations killed more than 1,000 Rohingya civilians, according to UN officials.<sup id="cite_ref-bad_to_worse_2017_09_06_washpost_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bad_to_worse_2017_09_06_washpost-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Independent2_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Independent2-7">[7]</a></sup> In August 2017, following attacks on local military outposts by Rohingya rebels, a resurgence in violence erupted throughout northern Rakhine. According to the UN and other agencies, the Myanmar military, aided by violent mobs of local Buddhist Rakhines killed over 400 people (whom the military claimed were "insurgents" or "terrorists"). Other estimates, including the UN's, estimate that at least 1,000 people were killed between 25 August and 8 September.<sup id="cite_ref-un_secretary_gen_2017_09_13_cnn_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un_secretary_gen_2017_09_13_cnn-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ben_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ben-9">[9]</a></sup> By September, the violence had resulted in 389,000 Rohingyas fleeing their homes.<sup id="cite_ref-un_says_389000_fled_2017_09_14_ap_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un_says_389000_fled_2017_09_14_ap-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Foreign leaders, including the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretary_General" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Secretary General">United Nations Secretary General</a> and other high UN officials, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> — while acknowledging the initial attack by Rohingya insurgents — have strongly criticized the Myanmar government's conduct in the current conflict, calling for the Myanmar government to restrain its forces and factions, and stop attacking civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-un_secretary_gen_2017_09_13_cnn_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un_secretary_gen_2017_09_13_cnn-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Rakhine_State_clashes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Rohingya_people" title="Rohingya people">Rohingya people</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rohingya_people" title="Rohingya people">Rohingya people</a> are an <a href="/wiki/Minority_group" title="Minority group">ethnic minority</a> that mainly live in the northern region of <a href="/wiki/Rakhine_State" title="Rakhine State">Rakhine State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>, and have been described as one of the world's most persecuted minorities.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-Who_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-Who-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TI-UN-Kyi_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TI-UN-Kyi-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IBT-1250_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IBT-1250-26">[26]</a></sup> They describe themselves as descendants of <a href="/wiki/Arab_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab people">Arab traders</a> and other groups who settled in the region many generations ago.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-Who_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-Who-24">[24]</a></sup> After riots in 2012, academic authors used the term Rohingya to refer to the Muslim community in northern Rakhine. For example, Professor Andrew Selth of <a href="/wiki/Griffith_University" title="Griffith University">Griffith University</a> uses "Rohingya" but states "These are Bengali Muslims who live in Arakan State...most Rohingyas arrived with the British colonialists in the 19th and 20th centuries."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeider20137_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeider20137-27">[27]</a></sup> Among the overseas Rohingya community, the term has been gaining popularity since the 1990s, though a considerable portion of Muslims in northern Rakhine are unfamiliar with the term and prefer to use alternatives.<sup id="cite_ref-Derek_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Derek-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-leider_arakan_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leider_arakan-29">[29]</a></sup> Scholars have stated that they have been present in the region since the 15th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Leider_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leider-30">[30]</a></sup> However, they have been denied citizenship by the government of Myanmar, which describes them as illegal immigrants from Bangladesh.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-Who_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-Who-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>In modern times, the <a href="/wiki/Persecution" title="Persecution">persecution</a> of Rohingyas in Myanmar dates back to the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-VOA_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VOA-31">[31]</a></sup> Since then, Rohingya people have regularly been made the target of persecution by the government and <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalist</a> <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GuardianUN_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuardianUN-20">[20]</a></sup> The tension between various religious groups in the country had often been exploited by the past military governments of Myanmar.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-Who_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-Who-24">[24]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>, the Rohingya have suffered from human rights violations under past <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship" title="Military dictatorship">military dictatorships</a> since 1978, and many have fled to neighbouring Bangladesh as a result.<sup id="cite_ref-Amn_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amn-32">[32]</a></sup> In 2005, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees</a> had assisted with the repatriation of Rohingyas from Bangladesh, but allegations of human rights abuses in the refugee camps threatened this effort.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> In 2015, 140,000 Rohingyas remained in <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_person" title="Internally displaced person">IDP</a> camps after <a href="/wiki/2012_Rakhine_State_riots" title="2012 Rakhine State riots">communal riots in 2012</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Timeline">Timeline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Rakhine_State_clashes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Timeline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016">2016</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Rakhine_State_clashes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2016">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Myanmar government claims that on 9 October, hundreds of unidentified insurgents attacked three Burmese border posts along Myanmar's border with Bangladesh. According to government officials in the majority Rohingya border town of <a href="/wiki/Maungdaw" title="Maungdaw">Maungdaw</a>, the attackers brandished knives, machetes and homemade slingshots that fired metal bolts. Several dozen firearms and boxes of ammunition were stolen by the attackers from the border posts. The attack resulted in the deaths of nine border officers.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC2_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC2-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RFA1_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RFA1-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC1_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC1-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reuters2_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters2-38">[38]</a></sup> Four Burmese soldiers were also killed two days later.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC3_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC3-39">[39]</a></sup> Government officials in <a href="/wiki/Rakhine_State" title="Rakhine State">Rakhine State</a> initially blamed the <a href="/wiki/Rohingya_Solidarity_Organisation" title="Rohingya Solidarity Organisation">Rohingya Solidarity Organisation</a> (RSO), an Islamist insurgent group mainly active in the 1980s and 1990s, for the attacks<sup id="cite_ref-AJ2_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AJ2-40">[40]</a></sup> but a group calling itself <a href="/wiki/Harakah_al-Yaqin" class="mw-redirect" title="Harakah al-Yaqin">Harakah al-Yaqin</a> (<i>Faith Movement</i>) later claimed responsibility.<sup id="cite_ref-BKP1_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BKP1-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the October incidents, the Myanmar Army began a major crackdown in the villages of northern Rakhine State. In the initial operation, dozens of people were killed and many were arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-Lady-CNN_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lady-CNN-42">[42]</a></sup> The military enforced a curfew and blocked food aid from the <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a> to 80,000 people in Rakhine State.<sup id="cite_ref-AJ19Oct2016_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AJ19Oct2016-43">[43]</a></sup> As the crackdown continued, the casualties increased. Arbitrary arrest, <a href="/wiki/Extrajudicial_killing" title="Extrajudicial killing">extrajudicial killings</a>, gang rapes, crimes against civilians, and <a href="/wiki/Looting" title="Looting">looting</a> were reportedly carried out.<sup id="cite_ref-Amnesty-Vicious_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amnesty-Vicious-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shoot-first_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shoot-first-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TI-UN-Kyi_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TI-UN-Kyi-25">[25]</a></sup> According to media reports, hundreds of Rohingya people had been killed by December 2016, and many had fled Myanmar as refugees to take shelter in the nearby areas of <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21000-rohingya_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21000-rohingya-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ethnic-cleansing_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnic-cleansing-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Aljazeera-humanity_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aljazeera-humanity-48">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IBT-1250_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IBT-1250-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lady-CNN_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lady-CNN-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Bundling_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This claim has too many footnotes for reading to be smooth. (September 2017)">excessive citations</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_police" title="Chief of police">chief of police</a> in Rakhine State, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sein_Lwin_(colonel)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sein Lwin (colonel) (page does not exist)">Sein Lwin</a>, announced on 2 November that his force had begun recruiting non-Rohingya locals for a new branch of "regional police", which would be trained in <a href="/wiki/Sittwe" title="Sittwe">Sittwe</a>, the capital of Rakhine State, and then sent back to their villages. The stated purpose of these forces was to defend villages against Rohingya insurgents; human rights organizations criticised the move as being likely to lead to further persecution of Rohingya civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-Jazeera1_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jazeera1-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reuters4_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters4-50">[50]</a></sup> New clashes began on 13 November, resulting in the deaths of one policeman, one soldier and six insurgents and the arrest of 36 suspected insurgents.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters2_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters2-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GD1_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GD1-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Fighting continued and on the third day of fighting, the death toll rose to 134 (102 insurgents and 32 security forces). The government later announced that 234 people suspected of being connected to the attack had been arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters1_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters1-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2017">2017</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Rakhine_State_clashes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2017">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_to_mid-2017">Early to mid-2017</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Rakhine_State_clashes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early to mid-2017">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Clashes between insurgents and the military continued in 2017. Burmese state media reported on 22 June that three insurgents had been killed by security forces in a raid on an insurgent camp supposedly belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Arakan_Rohingya_Salvation_Army" title="Arakan Rohingya Salvation Army">Arakan Rohingya Salvation Army</a> (ARSA), as part of a two-day "area clearance operation" by the government. Authorities confiscated gunpowder, ski masks and wooden rifles suspected to have been used for training.<sup id="cite_ref-ASEAN1_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASEAN1-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2017, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> accused Myanmar's military of mass killings and gang rapes, as well as burning down villages over the course of their "clearance operations". It stated that the military's operations had "likely" caused hundreds of deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Two senior UN officials working in its two separate agencies in Bangladesh stated that more than 1,000 may have died per testimonies gathered from Rohingyas. Meanwhile, Myanmar’s presidential spokesman, Zaw Htay said that per latest reports from military commanders, fewer than 100 people had been killed.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The Government of Myanmar denied that there was a systematic campaign of rape, though acknowledges it may have been committed by "individual members of the security forces".<sup id="cite_ref-MyanmarDeniesRape_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MyanmarDeniesRape-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>A police document obtained by <a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a> in March listed 423 Rohingyas detained by the police since 9 October 2016, 13 of whom were children, the youngest being ten years old. Two police captains in Maungdaw verified the document and justified the arrests, with one of them saying, "We the police have to arrest those who collaborated with the attackers, children or not, but the court will decide if they are guilty; we are not the ones who decide." Myanmar police also claimed that the children had confessed to their alleged crimes during interrogations, and that they were not beaten or pressured during questioning. The average age of those detained is 34, the youngest is 10, and the oldest is 75.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters3_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters3-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Star1_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Star1-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rakhine State police chief Sein Lwin announced on 27 June that security forces were on "high alert" after "masked assailants" killed several local administrators close to the Burmese government in the days prior.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> A week later on 4 July, a mob of at least a hundred <a href="/wiki/Rakhine_people" title="Rakhine people">Rakhine</a> <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhists</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sittwe" title="Sittwe">Sittwe</a> attacked seven Rohingya men from Dapaing camp for <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_person" title="Internally displaced person">internally displaced persons</a> with bricks,<sup id="cite_ref-Independent_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Independent-58">[58]</a></sup> killing one and severely injuring another. The Rohingya men were being escorted by police to Sittwe's docks to purchase boats, but were attacked despite armed guards being present nearby.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> According to a spokesman for the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Home_Affairs_(Myanmar)" title="Ministry of Home Affairs (Myanmar)">Burmese Ministry of Home Affairs</a>, an unarmed junior policeman was with the Rohingya men at the time of the attack, but was unable to stop the attackers.<sup id="cite_ref-Independent_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Independent-58">[58]</a></sup> One man was arrested in relation to the attacks on 26 July.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bodies of slain locals have been discovered over the course of the conflict; the government has stated that they were victims of Rohingya insurgents. The bodies of three Rohingya locals who had worked closely with the local administration were found in shallow graves in Maungdaw on 21 January. The government suspected that they were murdered by Rohingya insurgents in a reprisal attack.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Three decapitated bodies were found in <a href="/wiki/Rathedaung_Township" title="Rathedaung Township">Rathedaung Township</a> on 31 July. According to a government official, they were murdered by Rohingya insurgents.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> The bodies of six ethnic <a href="/wiki/Mro_people" title="Mro people">Mro</a> farmers, reportedly killed by Rohingya insurgents, were found in Maungdaw Township on 3 August.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="25_August_2017_ARSA_attacks">25 August 2017 ARSA attacks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Rakhine_State_clashes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 25 August 2017 ARSA attacks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The government announced on 25 August that 71 people (one soldier, one immigration officer, 10 policemen and 59 insurgents) had been killed overnight during coordinated attacks by up to 150 insurgents on 24 police posts and the 552nd Light Infantry Battalion army base in Rakhine State.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC4_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC4-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AP1_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP1-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reuters6_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters6-70">[70]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Myanmar_Army" title="Myanmar Army">Myanmar Army</a> stated that the attack began at around 1:00 AM, when insurgents armed with bombs, light weapons and machetes blew up a bridge. The army further stated that a majority of the attacks occurred around 3:00 AM to 4:00 AM.<sup id="cite_ref-at_least_71_dead_2017_08_29_straits_times_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-at_least_71_dead_2017_08_29_straits_times-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>The ARSA claimed they were taking "defensive actions" in 25 different locations and accused government soldiers of raping and killing civilians. The group also claimed that <a href="/wiki/Rathedaung" title="Rathedaung">Rathedaung</a> had been under a blockade for more than two weeks, starving the Rohingya, and that the government forces were preparing to do the same in Maungdaw.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>Myanmar's civilian leader, Aung San Suu Kyi, sharply criticized the insurgent Rohingya attacks as an attempt to undermine others' efforts to "build peace and harmony in Rakhine state."<sup id="cite_ref-pope_laments_2017_08_27_ap_foxnews_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pope_laments_2017_08_27_ap_foxnews-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span id="August–September_2017_crisis"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="August.E2.80.93September_2017_crisis">August–September 2017 crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Rakhine_State_clashes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: August–September 2017 crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Following the ARSA attacks of 25 August, the Myanmar military led a crackdown against the Rohingya in Rakhine state. The military has referred to the action as "clearance operations".<sup id="cite_ref-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news-73">[73]</a></sup> However, the military is also believed to be targeting Rohingya civilians in an attempt to drive the Rohingya out of Myanmar.<sup id="cite_ref-myanmar_accused_2017_09_10_ap_chicago_tribune_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_accused_2017_09_10_ap_chicago_tribune-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hundreds_dead_2017_09_10_washpost_chg_trib_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hundreds_dead_2017_09_10_washpost_chg_trib-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TroopsOpenFire_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TroopsOpenFire-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>On August 26, Myanmar troops opened fire on Rohingya civilians as they attempted to escape into Bangladesh.<sup id="cite_ref-TroopsOpenFire_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TroopsOpenFire-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DW_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DW-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>The violence resulted in the deaths of hundreds of people in Myanmar's Rakhine state. At least 1,000 have been killed as of September 7, according to <a href="/wiki/Yanghee_Lee" title="Yanghee Lee">Yanghee Lee</a>, the United Nations Special Rapporteur on Human Rights for Myanmar. She added that the figure is "very likely an underestimate".<sup id="cite_ref-Ben_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ben-9">[9]</a></sup> On the same day the Burmese military acknowledged "nearly 400" deaths,<sup id="cite_ref-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hundreds_dead_2017_09_10_washpost_chg_trib_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hundreds_dead_2017_09_10_washpost_chg_trib-75">[75]</a></sup> but claimed they were mostly "terrorists" or "militants." However, Rohingya accounts indicate that most of the dead were non-combatant civilians, including women and children.<sup id="cite_ref-hundreds_dead_2017_09_10_washpost_chg_trib_75-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hundreds_dead_2017_09_10_washpost_chg_trib-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bad_to_worse_2017_09_06_washpost_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bad_to_worse_2017_09_06_washpost-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rohingya refugees quickly began fleeing Myanmar by the thousands,<sup id="cite_ref-minorities_flee_2017_08_30_cbs_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-minorities_flee_2017_08_30_cbs-78">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news-73">[73]</a></sup> then, within two weeks, by the hundreds of thousands.<sup id="cite_ref-rohingya_have_fled_2017_09_08_ny_times_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rohingya_have_fled_2017_09_08_ny_times-79">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-unhcr_reports_2017_09_08_ap_fox_news_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unhcr_reports_2017_09_08_ap_fox_news-80">[80]</a></sup> By September 12, authorities in Bangladesh and aid agencies were reporting 370,000 refugees had fled Myanmar, mostly Rohingya Muslims (about a third of the estimated Rohingya population in Myanmar),<sup id="cite_ref-textbook_example_2017_09_12_wash_post_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-textbook_example_2017_09_12_wash_post-81">[81]</a></sup> but also hundreds of Hindus and Buddhists.<sup id="cite_ref-chicago_tribune_ap_26_dead_2017_08_31_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chicago_tribune_ap_26_dead_2017_08_31-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rohingya refugees arrived in Bangladesh with many injuries among them, including bullet wounds, and reported fleeing indiscriminate shootings, rapes, torture and other violent acts against Rohingya civilians<sup id="cite_ref-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news_73-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-myanmar_accused_2017_09_10_ap_chicago_tribune_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_accused_2017_09_10_ap_chicago_tribune-74">[74]</a></sup> by mobs of Buddhist Rakhine civilians and Myanmar government forces,<sup id="cite_ref-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news_73-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news-73">[73]</a></sup> including upon whole villages,<sup id="cite_ref-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news_73-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news-73">[73]</a></sup> many of which were burnt down<sup id="cite_ref-hundreds_dead_2017_09_10_washpost_chg_trib_75-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hundreds_dead_2017_09_10_washpost_chg_trib-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news_73-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news-73">[73]</a></sup> (reportedly some with villagers, even children, confined in the burning structures by their attackers).<sup id="cite_ref-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news_73-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>When <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> published satellite photos showing villages on fire,<sup id="cite_ref-satellite_data_2017_08_29_human_rights_watch_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-satellite_data_2017_08_29_human_rights_watch-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-satellite_images_2017_09_02_human_rights_watch_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-satellite_images_2017_09_02_human_rights_watch-84">[84]</a></sup> the Burmese government acknowledged that Rohingya houses were burned, but again insisted (as they did in 2012) that the Rohingya insurgents were burning their own villages.<sup id="cite_ref-hundreds_dead_2017_09_10_washpost_chg_trib_75-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hundreds_dead_2017_09_10_washpost_chg_trib-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news_73-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news-73">[73]</a></sup> However, a group of reporters, on a government-guided tour, apparently caught Rakhine civilians torching empty Rohingya houses,<sup id="cite_ref-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news_73-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news-73">[73]</a></sup> and one reporter was told by a Rakhine civilian that the police had assisted them.<sup id="cite_ref-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news_73-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_fires_2017_09_07_ap_abc_news-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>The U.N. High Commissioner for Human Rights said the violence appeared to be "a textbook example of 'ethnic cleansing.'"<sup id="cite_ref-textbook_example_2017_09_12_wash_post_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-textbook_example_2017_09_12_wash_post-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>Starting 6 September, reports emerged of Mynamar military had begun laying landmines near the border with Bangladesh.<sup id="cite_ref-MiningBorder_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MiningBorder-85">[85]</a></sup> Bangladesh said it had photographic evidence of Myanmar laying mines,<sup id="cite_ref-AlJazeeraMines_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlJazeeraMines-86">[86]</a></sup> and lodged an official complaint.<sup id="cite_ref-MiningBorder_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MiningBorder-85">[85]</a></sup> Though Myanmar had laid mines in the area in the 1990s, it denied laying mines recently. (<a href="/wiki/Ottawa_Treaty" title="Ottawa Treaty">Laying of landmines became illegal under international law</a> in 1997). On 10 September, Amnesty International accused Myanmar of laying mines.<sup id="cite_ref-rohingyas_crisis_landmines_2017_09_12_bbc_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rohingyas_crisis_landmines_2017_09_12_bbc-87">[87]</a></sup> The purpose of laying mines is believed to be to prevent the Rohingya refugees from returning.<sup id="cite_ref-AlJazeeraMines_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlJazeeraMines-86">[86]</a></sup> At least three people, including two children, had been injured in landmines as of 10 September.<sup id="cite_ref-myanmar_accused_2017_09_10_ap_chicago_tribune_74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_accused_2017_09_10_ap_chicago_tribune-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rohingyas_crisis_landmines_2017_09_12_bbc_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rohingyas_crisis_landmines_2017_09_12_bbc-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>A one-month unilateral ceasefire was declared by the ARSA on 9 September, in an attempt to allow aid groups and humanitarian workers safe access into northern Rakhine State.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JZceasefire_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JZceasefire-89">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBCceasefire_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCceasefire-90">[90]</a></sup> In a statement, the group urged the government to lay down their arms and agree to their ceasefire, which would have been in effect from 10 September until 9 October (the one-year anniversary of the first attacks on Burmese security forces by the ARSA). The government rejected the ceasefire, saying that they do not "negotiate with terrorists". Zaw Htay, the spokesperson for the State Counsellor's office, stated, "We have no policy to negotiate with terrorists."<sup id="cite_ref-hundreds_dead_2017_09_10_washpost_chg_trib_75-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hundreds_dead_2017_09_10_washpost_chg_trib-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CNNceasefire_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNNceasefire-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 17 September 2017, as the violence and flight of refugees continued, with the Myanmar government reporting 176 of 471 Rohingya villages abandoned. 430,000 Rohingya had reportedly fled into neighboring Bangladesh. Bangladesh announced plans to build shelters for 400,000 refugees and start immunizations, but began restricting their movements.<sup id="cite_ref-bangladesh_restricts_2017_09_17_wash_post_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bangladesh_restricts_2017_09_17_wash_post-92">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-myanmar_army_says_2017_09_17_bbc_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_army_says_2017_09_17_bbc-93">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-we_will_kill_you_all_2017_09_17_reuters_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-we_will_kill_you_all_2017_09_17_reuters-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretary_General" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Secretary General">United Nations Secretary General</a> <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres" title="António Guterres">António Guterres</a> urged Myanmar State Counsellor Suu Kyi to use her planned speech to her nation, 19 September to stop the offensive, warning that if she did not, "I don't see how this can be reversed in the future".<sup id="cite_ref-myanmar_army_says_2017_09_17_bbc_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_army_says_2017_09_17_bbc-93">[93]</a></sup> However, U.S. diplomats — while demanding that "this persecution must stop", attempted to be supportive of Suu Kyi's fragile, new civilian-leader position in a nation still largely ruled by the military.<sup id="cite_ref-myanmar_army_says_2017_09_17_bbc_93-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_army_says_2017_09_17_bbc-93">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bangladesh_restricts_2017_09_17_wash_post_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bangladesh_restricts_2017_09_17_wash_post-92">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-we_will_kill_you_all_2017_09_17_reuters_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-we_will_kill_you_all_2017_09_17_reuters-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-myanmar_faces_2017_09_17_reuters_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_faces_2017_09_17_reuters-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-secretaries_2017_09_17_cspan_org_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-secretaries_2017_09_17_cspan_org-96">[96]</a></sup> Suu Kyi's speech was later criticized by <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> as “a mix of untruths and victim-blaming”.<sup id="cite_ref-eco1_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eco1-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bangladesh meanwhile in August 2017 proposed joint military operations with Myanmar against ARSA.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> In September 2017, it accused Myanmar of repeatedly violating its <a href="/wiki/Airspace" title="Airspace">airspace</a> and issued a warning stating that any more "provocative acts" could have "unwarranted consequences". Myanmar spokesman, Zaw Htay, stated Myanmar would check any information Bangladesh provided.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Humanitarian_crisis">Humanitarian crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Rakhine_State_clashes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Humanitarian crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Displaced_Hindu_families_at_a_makeshift_camp_in_Maungdaw_(Moe_Zaw-VOA).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Displaced_Hindu_families_at_a_makeshift_camp_in_Maungdaw_%28Moe_Zaw-VOA%29.jpg/240px-Displaced_Hindu_families_at_a_makeshift_camp_in_Maungdaw_%28Moe_Zaw-VOA%29.jpg" width="240" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Displaced_Hindu_families_at_a_makeshift_camp_in_Maungdaw_%28Moe_Zaw-VOA%29.jpg/360px-Displaced_Hindu_families_at_a_makeshift_camp_in_Maungdaw_%28Moe_Zaw-VOA%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Displaced_Hindu_families_at_a_makeshift_camp_in_Maungdaw_%28Moe_Zaw-VOA%29.jpg/480px-Displaced_Hindu_families_at_a_makeshift_camp_in_Maungdaw_%28Moe_Zaw-VOA%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Displaced_Hindu_families_at_a_makeshift_camp_in_Maungdaw_(Moe_Zaw-VOA).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Displaced <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Myanmar" title="Hinduism in Myanmar">Hindu</a> families at a makeshift camp in Maungdaw.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>4,000 non-Muslim villagers were evacuated by security forces in late-August amid ongoing clashes. According to estimates by <a href="/wiki/Rohingya_refugees_in_Bangladesh" title="Rohingya refugees in Bangladesh">Rohingya refugees living in Bangladesh</a>, around 2,000 people crossed into Bangladesh.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> The number of displaced non-Muslims later rose to 30,000 in early-September.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> According to the United Nations, at least 270,000 Rohingya fled to Bangladesh in just two weeks following renewed violence that began on 25 August 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Exodus_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Exodus-102">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ben_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ben-9">[9]</a></sup> Prior to which, two refugee camps in <a href="/wiki/Cox%27s_Bazar" title="Cox's Bazar">Cox's Bazar</a> in Bangladesh were already home to nearly 34,000 Rohingya refugees.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-103">[103]</a></sup> On 1 September 2017, the bodies of 46 fleeing Rohingyas were found along the <a href="/wiki/Naf_River" title="Naf River">Naf River</a> after their boat capsized in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> On 6 September 2017, at least five children drowned when a Rohingya refugee boat sank at the mouth of the Naf river.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Some 23,000 others remain internally displaced within Rakhine State.<sup id="cite_ref-reliefweb_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2017, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Bangladesh" title="Government of Bangladesh">government of Bangladesh</a> announced that it planned to relocate the new refugees and another 232,000 Rohingya refugees already in the country to <a href="/wiki/Thengar_Char" title="Thengar Char">Thengar Char</a>, a sedimentary island in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bangladeshbbc_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bangladeshbbc-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bangladeshaj_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bangladeshaj-108">[108]</a></sup> The island first appeared around 2007, formed from washed down <a href="/wiki/Silt" title="Silt">silt</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Meghna_River" title="Meghna River">Meghna River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bangladeshbbc_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bangladeshbbc-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bangladeshaj_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bangladeshaj-108">[108]</a></sup> The nearest inhabited land, <a href="/wiki/Hatiya_Island" title="Hatiya Island">Hatiya Island</a> is around 30 kilometres (19&#160;mi) away.<sup id="cite_ref-bangladeshbbc_107-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bangladeshbbc-107">[107]</a></sup> News agencies quoted a regional official describing the plan as "terrible".<sup id="cite_ref-bangladeshaj_108-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bangladeshaj-108">[108]</a></sup> The move has received substantial opposition from a number of quarters. Human rights groups have described the plan as a forced relocation.<sup id="cite_ref-bangladeshaj_108-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bangladeshaj-108">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bangladeshbbc_107-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bangladeshbbc-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hundreds of <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Myanmar" title="Hinduism in Myanmar">Hindus</a> have also migrated to Bangladesh along with Rohingyas and complained of violence on their villages.<sup id="cite_ref-join_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-join-109">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BdNews_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BdNews-110">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DailyStar_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DailyStar-111">[111]</a></sup> From 25 August 2017, when the <a href="/wiki/Tatmadaw" title="Tatmadaw">Tatmadaw</a> (Myanmar Armed Forces) launched their <a href="/wiki/Military_operation" title="Military operation">military operation</a> in response to attacks by Rohingya militants, to 22 September 2017, satellite images showed that Rohingya villages were still being burned and an estimated 429,000 refugees had fled into <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> (creating a larger weekly outflow of refugees than the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_genocide" title="Rwandan genocide">Rwandan genocide</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-eco1_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eco1-97">[97]</a></sup> out of a pre-violence Rohingya population of about 1 million in Rakhine state.<sup id="cite_ref-eco1_97-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eco1-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Advisory_Commission_on_Rakhine_State">Advisory Commission on Rakhine State</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Rakhine_State_clashes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Advisory Commission on Rakhine State">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b> with: 2017 report. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Northern_Rakhine_State_clashes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(September 2017)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In August 2016, former <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">UN Secretary-General</a> <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a> was invited to head the <a href="/wiki/Advisory_Commission_on_Rakhine_State" title="Advisory Commission on Rakhine State">Advisory Commission on Rakhine State</a>, which was responsible for addressing human rights violations in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The complete report was published a year later by the Kofi Annan Foundation and accepted by the government of Myanmar in August 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> in which it cited 10% of the world's stateless people as having originated from Rakhine State.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> One of Kofi Annan's final statements after completing the commission's mandate was this:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>We propose a ministerial-level appointment to be made with the sole function of coordinating policy on Rakhine State and ensuring the effective implementation of the Rakhine Advisory Commission's recommendations. The appointee should be supported by a permanent and well-staffed secretariat, which will be an integral part of the Central Committee on Implementation of Peace and Development in Rakhine State and support its work.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>The Rakhine Commission released its report on 25 August, the same day new clashes erupted in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-at_least_71_dead_2017_08_29_straits_times_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-at_least_71_dead_2017_08_29_straits_times-71">[71]</a></sup> Massive retaliatory Burmese military attacks and Buddhist mob attacks ensued, leading to a further escalation in the regional humanitarian crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-what_is_going_on_2017_09_13_sydney_herald_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-what_is_going_on_2017_09_13_sydney_herald-117">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-new_committee_2017_09_13_ap_foxnews_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_committee_2017_09_13_ap_foxnews-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the deaths of over a thousand civilians in the ensuing violence and the exodus of over 350,000 Rohingya refugees, the office of the President of Myanmar announced on 12 September that it had formed a new 15-member committee to implement the recommendations of the Rakhine Commission.<sup id="cite_ref-new_committee_2017_09_13_ap_foxnews_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_committee_2017_09_13_ap_foxnews-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Implementation Committee of Rakhine Advisory Committee</i>, the president's office stated, was formed to adhere to the recommendations set for improving the security, social affairs and economic development of Myanmar's ethnic Rohingya Muslim minority, improving the sustainability of ethnic villages, removing camps for the displaced and accelerating the citizen verification process for Rohingyas under Myanmar's citizenship laws.<sup id="cite_ref-new_committee_2017_09_13_ap_foxnews_118-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_committee_2017_09_13_ap_foxnews-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights_violations">Human rights violations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Rakhine_State_clashes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Human rights violations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rohingya_persecution_in_Myanmar_(2016%E2%80%93present)" title="Rohingya persecution in Myanmar (2016–present)">Rohingya persecution in Myanmar (2016–present)</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arson">Arson</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Rakhine_State_clashes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Arson">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Burnt_down_house_in_northern_Rakhine_State_(Moe_Zaw-VOA).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Burnt_down_house_in_northern_Rakhine_State_%28Moe_Zaw-VOA%29.jpg/230px-Burnt_down_house_in_northern_Rakhine_State_%28Moe_Zaw-VOA%29.jpg" width="230" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Burnt_down_house_in_northern_Rakhine_State_%28Moe_Zaw-VOA%29.jpg/345px-Burnt_down_house_in_northern_Rakhine_State_%28Moe_Zaw-VOA%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Burnt_down_house_in_northern_Rakhine_State_%28Moe_Zaw-VOA%29.jpg/460px-Burnt_down_house_in_northern_Rakhine_State_%28Moe_Zaw-VOA%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Burnt_down_house_in_northern_Rakhine_State_(Moe_Zaw-VOA).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A burnt down house in a Rohingya village in northern Rakhine State.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Arakan_Rohingya_Salvation_Army" title="Arakan Rohingya Salvation Army">Arakan Rohingya Salvation Army</a> (ARSA) have been accused by the <a href="/wiki/State_Counsellor_of_Myanmar" title="State Counsellor of Myanmar">State Counsellor's</a> office of committing <a href="/wiki/Arson" title="Arson">arson</a> on <a href="/wiki/Kyaung" title="Kyaung">Buddhist monasteries</a> and local police outposts, killing innocent civilians and planting landmines. The ARSA has meanwhile accused <a href="/wiki/Myanmar_Army" title="Myanmar Army">Myanmar Army</a> of using civilians as human shields.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>A number of Rohingya properties were set alight during the violence, with residents blaming security forces while the government blamed Rohingya insurgents, suggesting that they had burnt down their own community's property.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> According to the State Counsellor's office, insurgents had burnt down 88 homes, more than 100 shops, two mosques and eight religious schools, as well as vehicles in a village.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Xinhua_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhua-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> in August 2017 said that satellite images showed widespread burning in 10 areas in northern Rakhine. While the causes of the fires could not be determined, the group said that it "compared the locations of these fires with witness statements it has collected and media reports, and found a correlation with some reported incidents where residences have allegedly been deliberately burned."<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>Chris Lewa, director of The Arakan Project, has blamed the security forces of burning village after village in a systematic way while also blaming Rohingya arsonists of burning the Buddhist village of Pyu Ma.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>'s crisis response director Tirana Hassan said that evidence points to Myanmar security setting northern Rakhine ablaze. The group also stated that it has credible reports of Rohingya militants burning the homes of ethnic Rakhine and other minorities.<sup id="cite_ref-Australian_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Australian-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Violence_towards_civilians">Violence towards civilians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Rakhine_State_clashes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Violence towards civilians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There were also reports of mass killings of Rohingyas by the military and Buddhist vigilantes in Chut Pyin village near Rathedaung. Lewa stated that they had received reports of 130 being killed in the village. A video provided to <a href="/wiki/ABC_News" title="ABC News">ABC News</a> by a human rights monitor purportedly shows the village burning and in another clip of freshly dug earth mound, allegedly graves of those killed.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Bangladesh's <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Bangladesh)" title="Minister of Foreign Affairs (Bangladesh)">Foreign Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Abul_Hassan_Mahmud_Ali" title="Abul Hassan Mahmud Ali">Abul Hassan Mahmud Ali</a> meanwhile has stated that Myanmar's security forces have killed over 3,000 Rohingyas during the 2017 clashes.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>Myanmar's military on September 24 stated that it found mass-graves of 28 Hindus whom it accused Rohingya militants of killing in Ye Baw Kya village a month eariler.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> Government spokesman Zaw Htay on the next day stated 17 more bodies had been found.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> An ARSA spokesman meanwhile denied the allegation that it was behind the killings and accused Buddhist nationalists of spreading lies to divide Hindus and Muslims.<sup id="cite_ref-BawKya_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BawKya-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some members of the Hindu community have also fled to Bangladesh with some blaming soldiers or Buddhist vigilantes for violence against them while others have accused the Rohingya insurgents of attacking them on suspicion of being government spies.<sup id="cite_ref-BawKya_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BawKya-130">[130]</a></sup> Some of the Hindus who migrated to Bangladesh stated that their villages are also experiencing killings, torture and arson attacks like those of Rohingyas. 86 Hindus were killed by unidentified men in Myanmar according to the refugees and Rana Dasgupta, head of the <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Hindu_Buddhist_Christian_Unity_Council" title="Bangladesh Hindu Buddhist Christian Unity Council">Bangladesh Hindu Buddhist Christian Unity Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-join_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-join-109">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BdNews_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BdNews-110">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DailyStar_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DailyStar-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Burmese government and Rohingya advocates have both accused the other side of killing civilians. Advocates for the Rohingyas have claimed that many civilians have died in military attacks on villages. The government has accused the ARSA of killing civilians, including Hindus and Muslims, some of whom were suspected by the ARSA of being government informants.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Xinhua_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhua-122">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kyodo_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kyodo-132">[132]</a></sup> ARSA in a statement has dismissed government allegations against it as baseless, seeking to present its cause as a defense of Rohingya rights.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Border_Guards_Bangladesh" title="Border Guards Bangladesh">Border Guards Bangladesh</a> station chief of the Ghumdum border post in Bangladesh has accused Myanmar's military of firing on fleeing Rohingyas. An <a href="/wiki/Agence_France-Presse" title="Agence France-Presse">Agence France-Presse</a> reporter counted more than a dozen mortar shells and several heavy machine gun rounds fired by Burmese security forces on fleeing Rohingyas.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rape">Rape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Rakhine_State_clashes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Rape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Myanmar security forces have reportedly raped Rohingya women during the violence. In February 2017, the UN's Human Rights Office published a report accused the army and police forces in Myanmar of committing gang rapes against Rohingya women.<sup id="cite_ref-newsweekReport_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsweekReport-135">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MyanmarDeniesRape_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MyanmarDeniesRape-13">[13]</a></sup> Systemic rape of Rohingya women has also been reported by <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> and other NGOs. <a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-REUTERSrape_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-REUTERSrape-138">[138]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/IRIN" title="IRIN">IRIN</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-IRINrape_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRINrape-139">[139]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/NPR" title="NPR">NPR</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-NPRrape_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPRrape-140">[140]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Myanmar_Times" class="mw-redirect" title="Myanmar Times">Myanmar Times</a><sup id="cite_ref-JournalistFired_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JournalistFired-141">[141]</a></sup> have all published reports of rape. Myanmar denies that there is a systematic campaign of rape, though acknowledges it may have been committed by "individual members of the security forces".<sup id="cite_ref-MyanmarDeniesRape_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MyanmarDeniesRape-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Reports of rape began in October 2016. On October 27, the <i><a href="/wiki/Myanmar_Times" class="mw-redirect" title="Myanmar Times">Myanmar Times</a></i> published an article reporting "dozens" of rapes in northern Rakhine state.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JournalistFired_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JournalistFired-141">[141]</a></sup> The journalist who wrote that piece was later fired, allegedly due to government pressure.<sup id="cite_ref-JournalistFired_141-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JournalistFired-141">[141]</a></sup> On October 28, <a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a> interviewed eight women who reported being raped by soldiers at gun point.<sup id="cite_ref-REUTERSrape_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-REUTERSrape-138">[138]</a></sup> In April 2017, <a href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" class="mw-redirect" title="National Public Radio">National Public Radio</a> interviewed 12 women from different villages who all reported rape.<sup id="cite_ref-NPRrape_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPRrape-140">[140]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/IRIN" title="IRIN">IRIN</a> reported instances of rape in May 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-IRINrape_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRINrape-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>Myanmar military is known to have committed rapes before.<sup id="cite_ref-NPRrape_140-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPRrape-140">[140]</a></sup> It was widely reported that in 2011, <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a> herself said "In the areas of the ethnic nationalities, rape is rife. It is used as a weapon by armed forces to intimidate the ethnic nationalities."<sup id="cite_ref-IRINrape_139-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRINrape-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions">Reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Rakhine_State_clashes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The military crackdown on Rohingya people drew criticism from various quarters. On 30 December 2016, nearly two dozen prominent human rights activists, including <a href="/wiki/Malala_Yousafzai" title="Malala Yousafzai">Malala Yousafzai</a>, Archbishop <a href="/wiki/Desmond_Tutu" title="Desmond Tutu">Desmond Tutu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Branson" title="Richard Branson">Richard Branson</a>, called on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> to intervene and end the "ethnic cleansing and crimes against humanity" being perpetrated in northern Rakhine State.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN3_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN3-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> high officials, and international organizations such as the human rights group <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>, have labeled the military crackdown on the Rohingya minority as "<a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnic cleansing</a>", adding that the military had made the civilians a target of "a systematic campaign of violence".<sup id="cite_ref-Aljazeera-humanity_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aljazeera-humanity-48">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC-Who_24-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-Who-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2017, a government-appointed commission rejected allegations of human rights violations and <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnic cleansing</a>, calling them "exaggerations".<sup id="cite_ref-Jazeera2_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jazeera2-146">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reuters5_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters5-147">[147]</a></sup> In September 2017, Desmond Tutu wrote an open letter to <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a> urging her "to speak out for justice, human rights and the unity of your people".<sup id="cite_ref-Exodus_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Exodus-102">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ben_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ben-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Nobel Laureates Malala<sup id="cite_ref-why_wont_assk_act_2017_09_08_bbc_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-why_wont_assk_act_2017_09_08_bbc-148">[148]</a></sup> and Bishop Tutu again appealed to Aung San Suu Kyi to intercede on behalf of the Rohingya, and on 6 September 2017 <a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a> called for an end to "persecution" of the Rohingya.<sup id="cite_ref-pope_laments_2017_08_27_ap_foxnews_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pope_laments_2017_08_27_ap_foxnews-21">[21]</a></sup> On September 14, U.S. Secretary of State Rex Tillerson said, "I think it is important that the global community speak out in support of what we all know the expectation is for the treatment of people regardless of their ethnicity... This violence must stop, this persecution must stop."<sup id="cite_ref-myanmar_faces_2017_09_14_ap_foxnews_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_faces_2017_09_14_ap_foxnews-149">[149]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister of the United Kingdom</a> <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a>'s spokesman announced on September 19 that UK will stop training Myanmar's armed forces until the crisis is resolved.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_restrictions">Government restrictions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Rakhine_State_clashes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Government restrictions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Access to Rakhine State by journalists and observers has been restricted by the authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> Myanmar stated in mid-September that it does not bar aid workers from Rakhine, but authorities on ground might restrict access for security reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-Australian_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Australian-125">[125]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Doctors_Without_Borders" class="mw-redirect" title="Doctors Without Borders">Doctors Without Borders</a> urged Myanmar on 18 September to grant international humanitarian organisations unrestricted and independent access to the conflict zone. In a statement, the organisation said that its international staff had not been granted authorisation to visit the health facilities since the end of August, whilst the national staff was afraid to go work in the region, after Myanmar officials accused NGOs of colluding with the ARSA.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Misleading_images">Misleading images</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Rakhine_State_clashes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Misleading images">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Misleading images have been used alongside claims of violence in the conflict, both by the Rohingya and against them. The difficulty of checking authenticity of images has proven a challenge for researchers. In 2016, a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Commission_on_Human_Rights" title="United Nations Commission on Human Rights">United Nations Commission on Human Rights</a> report stated that it would not use any photograph or video that it had not taken itself.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> In August 2017, one of the images shared on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> by <a href="/wiki/Mehmet_%C5%9Eim%C5%9Fek" title="Mehmet Şimşek">Mehmet Şimşek</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Deputy_Prime_Minister_of_Turkey" title="Deputy Prime Minister of Turkey">Deputy Prime Minister of Turkey</a>, was of the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_genocide" title="Rwandan genocide">Rwandan genocide</a>. He later deleted the image and issued a correction.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> In September 2017, a photo emerged allegedly showing several Rohingyas setting fire to buildings in their own villages, but were two of the people pictured in the photo were later recognised as Hindus by journalists in a nearby school building. The <a href="/wiki/Eleven_Media_Group" title="Eleven Media Group">Eleven Media Group</a> published an article showing burned Rohingya homes in Ka Nyin Tan, with government spokesman Zaw Htay tweeting a link to it with the caption "Photos of Bengalis setting fire to their houses!". However, one person in the photos was later found at the public school housing shelter for displaced Hindus.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_reaction">International reaction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Rakhine_State_clashes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: International reaction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/International_reaction_to_the_2016%E2%80%9317_Rohingya_exodus" title="International reaction to the 2016–17 Rohingya exodus">International reaction to the 2016–17 Rohingya exodus</a></div>
<p>International condemnation of government and government-supported civilian attacks on Rohingyas and other minorities in the region led to widespread public protests around the world, in countries such as France and Indonesia.<sup id="cite_ref-protests_2017_09_08_cnn_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-protests_2017_09_08_cnn-156">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-horror_enraged_pakistanis_2017_09_12_washpost_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-horror_enraged_pakistanis_2017_09_12_washpost-157">[157]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-myanmar_faces_2017_09_10_wsj_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_faces_2017_09_10_wsj-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<p>The State Counsellor of Myanmar, <a href="/wiki/Aung_Sun_Suu_Kyi" class="mw-redirect" title="Aung Sun Suu Kyi">Aung Sun Suu Kyi</a>, has been criticised by the international community for not condemning the violence or the Burmese Army's military response to the crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-hundreds_dead_2017_09_10_washpost_chg_trib_75-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hundreds_dead_2017_09_10_washpost_chg_trib-75">[75]</a></sup> Aung San Suu Kyi was initially backed by the Indian Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Narendra_Modi" title="Narendra Modi">Narendra Modi</a>; however, the government of India quickly urged "restraint" in the "anti-terrorism" operations.<sup id="cite_ref-indian_pm_2017_09_06_cnn_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indian_pm_2017_09_06_cnn-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-india_urges_2017_09_10_wsj_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-india_urges_2017_09_10_wsj-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Rakhine_State_clashes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
